Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
15 min
Forms of Ima' through Differentiation (Al-Farq) in Hanafi Usul
Listing five linguistic forms for ima' through differentiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify five linguistic forms (description, goal, exception, condition, istidrak) that indicate causality through differentiation, and derive the 'illah (cause) from each using the Hanafi method of ima'.

Core Idea
Differentiation between two rulings paired with two descriptions uncovers the cause for each — a core Hanafi tool for extracting 'illah from the text.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, one of the ways to identify the cause ('illah) of a ruling is through 'ima' — a textual indication that does not explicitly say 'this is the cause' but strongly implies it. One powerful form of ima' is al-farq (differentiation): when the text contrasts two rulings against two distinct descriptions, it becomes clear that each description is the cause for its corresponding ruling. This lesson examines five linguistic forms through which such differentiation occurs, as presented in Fawatih al-Rahamut. Mastery of these forms trains you to read legal texts with precision and derive rulings with methodological rigor.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of ima' by farq
Recognize that when a text mentions two different rulings linked to two different descriptions, each description is likely the cause for its ruling. For example: 'For the pedestrian one share, for the horseman two shares' — here pedestrianism and horsemanship are the respective causes.
This is different from explicit causation statements like 'because of X'.
2
Identify the first form: two descriptions (صفة)
Look for two descriptive terms each assigned to a separate ruling. Example: 'The killer does not inherit' — the description 'killer' differentiates from other heirs who do inherit, indicating that the act of killing is the cause for exclusion from inheritance.
The text does not need to mention both descriptions in one sentence; the contrast is understood from the context.
3
Identify the second form: goal/limit (غاية)
When a ruling is linked to a limit like 'until they are purified' (حتى يطهرن), the limit differentiates the state before (impurity) from after (purity), indicating that purity is the cause for the change of ruling.
The Arabic word 'حتى' indicates the end point.
4
Identify the third form: exception (استثناء)
An exception like 'unless they forgive' in the verse on dowry differentiates between the general ruling (half is owed) and the excepted case (nothing if forgiven). Forgiveness is thus the cause for dropping the obligation.
The exception creates a clear contrast.
5
Identify the fourth form: condition (شرط)
A condition like 'when the types differ, then sell as you wish' in the riba hadith contrasts with the unconditional prohibition when types are the same. The condition of differing types is therefore the cause for permissibility.
The passage also refutes the Shafi'i view on the cause of riba, affirming the Hanafi position that the cause is unity of type plus standard measure, not taste or monetary value.
6
Identify the fifth form: istidrak (استدراك)
An exceptive particle like 'lakin' (but) differentiates two rulings. Example: 'Allah does not hold you accountable for unintentional oaths, BUT He holds you accountable for what your hearts have earned.' The contrast indicates that intention is the cause for expiation.
Istidrak is similar to exception but uses contrastive conjunctions.
7
Summarize the Hanafi method
These five forms demonstrate how Hanafi usul uses textual differentiation to infer causation. Recognizing these patterns is essential for qiyas (analogy) and for understanding rulings derived from texts.
The 'illah identified through these forms is considered a strong indication (ima') and is used in legal reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنه أي من الإيماء الفرق بين حكمين بوصفين فيعلم أن أحدهما علة لواحد والآخر لآخر (إما بصيغة صفة مثل) قوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم (للراجل سهم وللفارس سهمان) رواه الفقهاء وتكلم عليه بعض أهل الحديث، وتفصيله في فتح القدير، فهذا بعد صحته يدل على أن الفروسية علة لاستحقاق سهمين والرجالة لاستحقاق سهم (ومثل) قوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: «لا يرث القاتل» وهو حديث صحيح مشهور وقد ثبت أن غيره وارث) إذ كان معلوماً من الدين ضرورة توريث العصبات وغيرهم من ذوي الفروض فوقع الفرق بوصف القتل، فعلم أنه علة الحرمان وفيه إشارة إلى أنه لا يجب ذكر الوصفين في الكلام معاً (أو) بصيغة (غاية كحتى يطهرن) فإنه قد فرق فيه بالطهارة عن الحيض والنجاسة به فعلم أن الأول سبب الحرمة (أو) بصيغة (استثناء) نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿فَنِصْفُ مَا فَرَضْتُمْ إِلَّا أَن يَعْفُونَ ﴾ [البقرة: ۲۳۷] فوقع الفرق بالعفو ،وعدمه، فعلم أن العفو علة للسقوط ولك أن تقول قد وقع الفرق بين حكمي ولزوم الكامل بالعفو من الزوجة أو العفو من الزوج، كما في قوله تعالى : أو يَعْفُوا الَّذِي بِيَدِهِ، عُقْدَةُ النِكَاح ﴾ [البقرة: ۲۳۷] وهو عندنا الزوج فالعفو منها علة السقوط، ومنه علة اللزوم فتأمل فيه ( أو ) صيغة (شرط) نحو قوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: «الذهب بالذهب والفضة بالفضة والحنطة بالحنطة والشعير بالشعير والتمر بالتمر والزبيب بالزبيب مثلاً بمثل يداً بيد والفضل «ربا» و «إذا اختلف الجنسان) فبيعوا كيف شئتم رواه الأكثرون من أهل الحديث، فبإناطة الجواز باختلاف الجنس، وقد كانت الحرمة في متحد الجنس إلا متساوياً في المقياس علم أنه فارق فاختلاف الجنس يوجب الحل، إلا أن الأصل الحرمة والاختلاف مخلص كما عليه الشافعي على ما نقل مشايخنا عنه، واتحاد الجنس مع المعيار علة الحرمة، لا كما زعم الشافعي من علية الطعم أو الثمنية، ولا كما زعم علية الاقتيات (أو) بصيغة (استدراك) نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿لَّا يُؤَاخِذُكُمُ اللَّهُ بِاللَّغْوِ فِي أَيْمَانِكُمْ وَلَكِن يُؤَاخِذُكُم بِمَا كَسَبَتْ قُلُوبُكُمْ ( ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۲٥] فدل على أن المنعقدة علة الكفارة
And from it (i.e., from ima') is the differentiation between two rulings by two descriptions, so it is known that one is the cause for one and the other for the other. (Either in the form of a description like) his saying, peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions: 'For the pedestrian one share, and for the horseman two shares.' Reported by the jurists and discussed by some hadith scholars, and its detail is in Fath al-Qadir. So this, after its authenticity, indicates that horsemanship is the cause for entitlement to two shares and pedestrianism for entitlement to one share. (And like) his saying, peace and blessings be upon him: 'The killer does not inherit' — it is a sound and well-known hadith, and it is established that others are heirs, since it is known from the religion by necessity the inheritance of the agnates and others of the prescribed shares. So differentiation occurred by the description of killing, so it is known that it is the cause for deprivation. And in it is an indication that it is not necessary to mention both descriptions in the speech together. (Or) in the form of (a limit/goal like 'until they are purified') for it distinguishes by purification from menstruation and impurity, so it is known that the first is the cause of prohibition. (Or) in the form of (exception) like His saying, exalted: 'Then half of what you have fixed unless they forgive' [Quran 2:237]. So differentiation occurred by forgiveness and its absence, so it is known that forgiveness is the cause for dropping. But you may say: differentiation has occurred between two rulings: the obligation of half and the obligation of full [dower] by forgiveness from the wife or forgiveness from the husband, as in His saying: 'or forgives he in whose hand is the marriage knot' [Quran 2:237] and he is according to us the husband. So forgiveness from her is the cause for dropping, and from him the cause for obligation. So reflect on it. (Or) in the form of (condition) like his saying, peace and blessings be upon him: 'Gold for gold, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, raisins for raisins, like for like, hand to hand, and excess is usury' and 'When the types differ, then sell as you wish.' Reported by the majority of hadith scholars. So by linking permissibility to difference of type, while prohibition was in the same type except when equal in measure, it is known that it differentiated, so difference of type necessitates solution. However, the original [ruling] is prohibition and difference is an escape as according to al-Shafi'i according to what our shaykhs transmitted from him. And unity of type with the standard is the cause of prohibition, not as al-Shafi'i claimed of causality of taste or monetary value, nor as he claimed of causality of being a staple food. (Or) in the form of (istidrak/exceptive) like His saying, exalted: 'Allah does not hold you accountable for what is unintentional in your oaths, but He holds you accountable for what your hearts have earned' [Quran 2:225]. So it indicates that the binding oath is the cause for expiation.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage enumerates different linguistic forms through which ima' (indication of causality) occurs via differentiation between two rulings and two descriptions. The examples are: (1) Using two descriptions: the hadith of pedestrian and horseman shows that the description (pedestrian vs. horseman) causes the difference in shares. Also the hadith 'the killer does not inherit' differentiates between killer and other heirs. (2) Using a 'ghaya' (limit) like 'until they are purified' differentiates between menstruation and purity. (3) Using 'istithna' (exception) like the verse on dowry forgiveness indicates that forgiveness is the cause for dropping the obligation. (4) Using 'shart' (condition) like the hadith on riba stating that when types differ, sell as you wish, indicating that difference of type is the cause for permissibility, while unity of type is the cause for prohibition. The author refutes the Shafi'i position that taste or monetary value is the cause of riba. (5) Using 'istidrak' (exceptive) like the verse on oaths indicating that intentional oaths are the cause for expiation. This section demonstrates the Hanafi method of identifying the 'illah from textual indications.

Key Terms
الفرق (al-farq): The differentiation between two rulings by two descriptions, indicating that each description is the cause for its respective ruling.
الغاية (al-ghaya): A limit or goal that indicates causality by differentiating before and after it.
الاستثناء (al-istithna): Exception that differentiates between two rulings, indicating the cause for the exception.
الشرط (al-shart): Condition that differentiates between two rulings, indicating that the condition is the cause.
الاستدراك (al-istidrak): An exceptive or contrastive particle like 'lakin' that indicates a differentiation of rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the five linguistic forms of ima' through differentiation as listed in the passage?
A) صفة (description)
B) غاية (goal)
C) تمييز (discrimination)
D) شرط (condition)

Key Takeaway
Differentiation (al-farq) between two rulings by two descriptions is a powerful method of ima', and the Hanafi school uses five linguistic forms to extract the 'illah.

Munāsaba in Ima': Is Apparent Suitability Required?
Presenting the preferred view that suitability is necessary in reality but not for understanding ima'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the necessity of munāsaba in ima' and distinguish between suitability in reality and its apparentness for deriving causation.

Core Idea
Munāsaba is necessary in reality for a valid cause, but not required to be apparent when understanding ima'.

In this passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut, the author presents the preferred Hanafi view on the role of munāsaba (suitability) in ima'. While the connection between the description and ruling must be suitable in reality, the mujtahid does not need to explicitly know that suitability for the ima' to indicate causation. This distinction is crucial for understanding how causes ('illal) are identified in qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three opinions
List the three positions mentioned: the chosen view, the view requiring apparent suitability due to weak ima', and the view conditioning understanding from juxtaposition on suitability.
Focus on the reasoning behind each.
2
Analyze the chosen view's reasoning
Understand why the preferred view holds that ima' is complete and does not need external suitability to be apparent. The indication itself is sufficient.
This is a key Hanafi principle: the ima' is a full dalil.
3
Contrast with the alternative views
Compare the alternatives: one views ima' as weak and therefore requiring apparent suitability, the other conditions it on suitability even in juxtaposition.
Recognize that the difference stems from assumptions about the strength of ima'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ههنا نكات : النكتة الأولى القول المختار أن المناسبة بين الوصف المومىء إليه والحكم لا بد في الواقع إذ لا علة دونها أما ظهورها فليس بشرط في فهم التعليل من الإيماء لأن دلالة الإيماء تامة فلا ينظر إلى ما سواه من المناسبة وغيرها وقيل ظهور المناسبة شرط لضعف دلالة الإيماء لكونها من قرينة وقيل إن فهم التعليل من المقارنة بين الوصف والحكم اشترطت
Then here are points: The first point: The chosen opinion is that the suitability between the description indicated by ima' and the ruling is necessary in reality, for there is no cause without it. As for its apparentness, it is not a condition for understanding the derivation of causation from ima', because the indication of ima' is complete, so one does not look beyond it to suitability or other than it. And it was said that apparentness of suitability is a condition due to the weakness of the indication of ima' because it is from a clue. And it was said that understanding the derivation of causation from the juxtaposition of the description and the ruling is conditioned [by suitability].
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is a nukta (a subtle point) discussing the role of munāsaba (suitability) in the context of ima'. The preferred view (القول المختار) is that suitability between the description (which is the indicator of the cause) and the legal ruling is necessary in reality (في الواقع) — meaning that there can be no valid cause without an appropriate connection between the description and the ruling. However, this suitability does not need to be apparent or known for a mujtahid to understand the causation from the ima' itself, because the ima' provides a complete indication. So even if the suitability is not obvious, the ima' alone is sufficient. An opposing view holds that the suitability must be apparent because the ima' is weak (coming from a clue). Another view holds that understanding causation from juxtaposition requires the suitability to be conditioned. This is a key methodological point in Hanafi usul: while the 'illah must actually be suitable, the evidence for it (through ima') does not require the suitability to be manifest.

Key Terms
المناسبة (al-munāsaba): The logical suitability or appropriate connection between the description (wasf) and the ruling (hukm) that makes the description a valid cause.
الإيماء (al-īmā'): A type of indication (dalāla) where the ruling is juxtaposed with a description in a way that suggests the description is the cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen opinion in this passage, is the apparentness of munāsaba (suitability) a condition for understanding causation from ima'?
A) Yes, because ima' is weak
B) No, because ima' provides complete indication
C) Yes, because the cause must be suitable
D) No, because suitability is not needed at all

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi view: munāsaba is necessary in reality but not required to be apparent for ima' to indicate causation.

Imā' by Association (al-Iqtirān): Definition and Application
Defining imā' by association and analyzing two prophetic examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify an instance of imā' by association in a source text and explain how it differs from explicit textual indication.

Core Idea
Imā' by association infers causality from juxtaposition: shared attribute links the rulings.

In this passage, the author defines the subtle usul tool of imā' by association and tests it against two prophetic traditions. You will learn to recognize this indirect legal indication and see how scholars refine the cause (tanqīḥ al-manāṭ) to avoid superficial interpretations. The discussion reveals the rigour required to properly deploy this method of istidlal.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition
Identify the definition of imā' bi al-iqtirān: if the mentioned description or its counterpart were not the cause, the connection would be far-fetched.
Focus on 'counterpart' (nazīr) – the paired element.
2
Analyze the Khath'amiyya hadith
See how the Prophet mentions the slave's debt alongside the question about Hajj debt. The juxtaposition implies that the common attribute 'being a debt' is the cause for completion (ijzā').
Note the objection of Ibn al-Humām and the author's response about initial appearance vs. refined cause.
3
Understand tanqīḥ al-manāṭ
The passage shows that initial identification of the cause may be superficial; further refinement (tanqīḥ) is needed to isolate the true shared attribute.
This is crucial for correct application of imā'.
4
Examine the 'Umar example
The Prophet's response to 'Umar about kissing while fasting is presented. Some argue it is not imā' because it only negates invalidation, but the author defends it as a refutation of 'Umar's presumption, thereby still indicating causality.
Distinguish between direct causal indication and refutation of a false assumption.
5
Distinguish imā' from naṣṣ
Imā' is not an explicit text but a notification of the basis of qiyas. Recognize that it requires contextual sensitivity.
This places imā' in the hierarchy of proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النكتة (الثالثة: عرف الإيماء بالاقتران بما لو لم يكن هو أو نظيره علة كان بعيداً)، ومثل للثاني بحديث الخثعمية المذكور سابقاً فإنها سألته عن دين الله الذي هو الحج (فذكر) صلوات الله وسلامه عليه دين العبد ونبه على كونه علة للأجزاء) أي فراغ ذمة الأب عن دين العبد (ففهم أن المسؤول عنه وهو دين الله تعالى (كذلك) أي علة للإجزاء، فذكر دين العبد لكون نظيره، وهو دين الله علة الإجزاء (وأورد) الشيخ ابن الهمام أن العلة) ههنا (كون المقضى ديناً لا دين الله ولا دين العبد (وإنما ذكر النظير ليعلم أن الأمر (المشترك) بين المسؤول : وبين المذكور (علة) لا أن نظيره علة المسؤول (أقول) العلة في بادىء الرأي هو النظير) وهذا القدر يكفي لكونه إيماء، كما أن العلة في ظاهر الأمر الوقاع في حديث الأعرابي (وبعد التنقيح للمناط بحيث لا يرد النقض بالصلاة) فإنه لا تجزي صلاة رجل من غيره (يعلم علية الجنس) وهو كونه ديناً كما في قصة الأعرابي ظهر بعد التنقيح أن العلة الجناية الكاملة على الصوم (ولذلك يسمى مثله تنبيهاً على أصل القياس لا نصاً صريحاً، وقد يمثل بقوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم (العمر) أمير المؤمنين (وقد سأله عن قبلة الصائم هل تفسد الصوم (أرأيت) مقولة للقول (لو) تمضمضت بماء ثم مججته أيفسد وقيل على التمثيل ليس هذا تعليلاً لمنع الإفساد إذا ليس فيه ما يمنعه، إذ غايته أي غاية ما فيه (عدم ما يوجبه) أي ليس فيه شيء يوجب الإفساد ولا يلزم منه وجود ما يوجب عدمه فلم يكن فيه إيماء العلية أصلاً فليس من الباب أصلاً (بل) هو ) أي لو تمضمضت الخ ... نقض لما توهم) أمير المؤمنين (عمر أن كل مقدمة للمفسد مفسد ، كذا في «المختصر». أقول : التعليل مبني على أن الإفساد للصوم
The third subtle point: Imā' by association (iqtirān) is defined as that which, if it or its counterpart were not the cause, would be far-fetched. He exemplifies the second [counterpart] with the hadith of al-Khath'amiyya mentioned earlier: she asked him about the debt of Allah, which is Hajj, so he (peace and blessings be upon him) mentioned the debt of a slave and pointed out that it is the cause for completion, meaning the discharge of the father's liability from the slave's debt. So it was understood that what was asked about, namely the debt of Allah Almighty, is likewise a cause for completion. So he mentioned the slave's debt because its counterpart, namely the debt of Allah, is the cause for completion. And Shaykh Ibn al-Humām objected that the cause here is that what is paid off is a debt, not the debt of Allah nor the debt of a slave; he only mentioned the counterpart to show that the common factor between the asked and the mentioned is the cause, not that the counterpart is the cause of the asked. I say: at first glance, the cause is the counterpart, and this much suffices for it to be imā', just as the cause in the apparent case is intercourse in the hadith of the Bedouin. After tanqīḥ al-manāṭ such that refutation by prayer (salat) does not apply—for a man's prayer does not suffice for another—it is known that the genus is the cause, i.e., being a debt. Similarly, in the story of the Bedouin, after tanqīḥ it became clear that the cause is the complete offense against the fast. Therefore, such an example is called a notification of the basis of qiyas, not an explicit text. And it may be exemplified by his statement (peace be upon him) to 'Umar, the Commander of the Faithful, when he asked him about the kiss of a fasting person: does it invalidate the fast? 'Do you think that if you rinsed your mouth with water and then spat it out, would it invalidate?' It is said concerning this example: This is not a ta'līl for preventing invalidation, because there is nothing in it that prevents it; its utmost is the absence of what necessitates it. There is nothing in it that necessitates invalidation, and it does not necessarily follow that there is something that necessitates its absence. So it contains no imā' of causality at all, and thus it is not from this category at all. Rather, it is a refutation of what the Commander of the Faithful 'Umar presumed, that every preliminary to an invalidator is itself an invalidator. This is in al-Mukhtasar. I say: The ta'līl is based on that the invalidation of the fast is...
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage defines imā' by association (iqtirān) as an indirect indication where, if the mentioned description or its counterpart were not the cause, the connection would be far-fetched. Two examples are discussed. First, the hadith of al-Khath'amiyya: she asked about performing Hajj on behalf of her father; the Prophet mentioned paying off a slave's debt, implying that both are debts and thus the cause for discharge is 'being a debt.' Ibn al-Humām objected that the common factor is 'debt' itself, not the specific type. The author responds that initially, the counterpart appears to be the cause, which suffices for imā'. Second, the story of 'Umar asking about kissing while fasting: the Prophet gave the example of rinsing the mouth, which does not invalidate. Some say this is not imā' because it merely shows absence of invalidation, not the cause of non-invalidation. Others say it refutes 'Umar's presumption that any precursor to invalidation is itself invalidating. The passage illustrates the nuanced application of imā' and the need for further refinement (tanqīḥ).

Key Terms
إيماء بالاقتران (imā' bi al-iqtirān): An indirect indication of causality through association, where mentioning one thing alongside another implies that they share the same cause if the connection would otherwise be far-fetched.
تنقيح المناط (tanqīḥ al-manāṭ): The process of refining the effective cause by isolating the precise common attribute that justifies the ruling, eliminating irrelevant specifics.
نظير (nazīr): The counterpart or similar case mentioned alongside the case in question to indicate the common cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, after tanqīḥ al-manāṭ in the hadith of al-Khath'amiyya, what is identified as the actual cause for completion (ijzā')?
A) The specific debt of Allah (Hajj)
B) The specific debt of a slave
C) The common attribute of being a debt (al-dayn)
D) The act of asking a question

Key Takeaway
Imā' by association is a valid but subtle method of causal indication that requires careful refinement (tanqīḥ) to identify the true common attribute; it includes both positive juxtaposition and refutation of false assumptions.

Sabr wa Taqsim: Method and Hujjiyah
Explains sabr wa taqsim and its hujjiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the method of sabr wa taqsim, apply its three sub-methods of elimination, and evaluate the Hanafi position that it is not a valid proof without apparent effect.

Core Idea
Sabr wa taqsim is a disputed method; Hanafis reject it because elimination alone does not prove the remaining attribute is legally considered.

This passage presents the third maslak (method) for discovering the effective cause ('illa) in qiyas: sabr wa taqsim (division and elimination). It explains how to enumerate possible attributes, eliminate invalid ones, and thereby determine the 'illa. The author also details three specific ways to eliminate attributes—ilgha', tard, and lack of munasaba—and then surveys the major schools' positions on whether this method constitutes a valid proof (hujja). As a Hanafi usul student, you need to understand both the technique and why the majority of Hanafis consider it insufficient unless supported by apparent effect.

Guided Path
1
Define sabr wa taqsim
State the meaning: enumerating all attributes suitable for causality and eliminating those that are invalid, leaving the claimed 'illa as the only remaining attribute.
The method yields a presumption (zann) of causality, not certainty.
2
Identify the three sub-methods of elimination
Learn ilgha' (showing the ruling persists without the eliminated attribute), tardiyya (proving the attribute is casually irrelevant), and lack of munasaba (no apparent suitability). Each provides a way to discard invalid attributes.
Ilgha' negates partiality of the eliminated attribute; tardiyya asserts the attribute is not considered by the Lawgiver at all or in this ruling.
3
Understand the conditions for valid sabr wa taqsim
The viewer must be 'adl (upright) and conduct thorough investigation (istiqra'). If the opponent presents an equivalent attribute, the viewer must invalidate it to maintain the claim.
Mere enumeration without evidence of a new attribute does not invalidate the method.
4
List the four positions on hujjiyah
The passage records: (1) Most Shafi'is and Malikis: proof for both parties; (2) Most Hanafis: not a proof at all; (3) Imam al-Haramayn: proof if the original's 'illa is based on consensus; (4) Some: proof for the viewer only, not the opponent.
The Hanafi position (except al-Jassas and al-Marghinani) is the most restrictive.
5
Analyze the Hanafi objection
Hanafis argue that the remaining attribute has not been proven valid by the Law (shar') because its effect (ta'thir) is not apparent. Mere elimination does not show that the Lawgiver actually considers it.
This highlights the Hanafi emphasis on explicit legal effect over logical presumption.

من هذا (و) المسلك الثالث : السبر والتقسيم وهو حصر الأوصاف الصالحة للعلية (وحذف ما سوى) الوصف (المدعي) عليته يعني إبطاله (فيتعين) المدعي (ولا يمنع الحصر مجرداً) عن الاستناد بأحداث وصف آخر (لأن الناظر المدعي للحصر (عدل) فيقبل قوله لأنه إنما حكم بعد الاستقراء البالغ، وإذا لم يجد بعد الاستقراء ظن بالحصر وليس المقصود القطع حتى يمنع بعد حصول الظن وفيه تأمل فتأمل (و) لأن الأصل) (العدم لغيره من الأوصاف، وهذا أوهن من بيت العنكبوت كما لا يخفى (بل) إنما يمنع الحصر مستنداً بإبداء وصف فعليه إبطاله) إتماماً لاستدلاله ولا يلزم انقطاعه عن البحث (على) القول (المختار لأن الحصر ظني) فلا مضايقة في ظهور وصف آخر على أن الوصف الباطل كالمعدوم فلا يضر الحصر ولا ينقطع البحث في «الحاشية»، قال السبكي وعندي ينقطع إذا كان ما اعترض به مساوياً لما ذكره في الحصر وأبطله ، وفيه أن له أن يقول لما كان مساوياً لما أبطلته ما ذكرته فإن قلت : لعل غرضه أنه لما أبدى وصفاً مساوياً، فقد اعترض على دليل الإبطال، فلا يصح تركه للبطلان، قلت له أن يقول لما كان باطلاً هو عندي تركته. وإذ قد أبديت الآن أشمر ذيلي للأبطال فتأمل فيه . (ثم للحذف طرق منها الإلغاء وهو بيان الحكم بالباقي) الذي هو المدّعي (فقط) من غير شركة آخر (في محل ما وهو الذي لا يوجد فيه أوصاف أخر فيعلم أن المحذوف لا دخل له) في الحكم بالمشاركة مع الباقي فإن قلت حاصل هذا يرجع إلى أن المحذوف لو كان علة لانتفى الحكم بانتفائه مع أنه يثبت الحكم مع انتفاء الأوصاف المحذوفة وحينئذ يلزم اشتراط العكس. أجاب ولا يلزم العكس لأن (المراد ههنا بالإلغاء (نفي الجزئية) فحاصله يرجع إلى أن المحذوف ليس جزء للباقي وإلا ثبت الحكم به فقط في هذا المحل فلا يلزم منه العكس، إنما يلزم لو أريد إبطال استقلال المحذوف (قيل) إذا كان الباقي وجد في محل بدون الأوصاف الملغاة فالقياس على ذلك المحل يسقط مؤنة الإلغاء) فليقس أوّلاً عليه، فاستعمال السبر والتقسيم مما لا طائل تحته ويدفع بأنه أي القياس على ذلك المحل (لا يستمر إذ ربما كان أوصافه أكثر من الأصل المفروض، فلا بد لإبطاله من استعمال تقسيم وإلغاء ويؤدّي إلى التطويل (ومنها) أي من طرق الحذف (الطردية) أي بيان أن الأوصاف طردية أي ملغاة لم يعتبرها الشارع (إما مطلقاً) أي ملغاة عنده رأساً في الأحكام كلها كالطول والقصر أو في) الحكم المبحوث عنه كالذكورة والأنوثة في أحكام العتق ومنها أي من طرق الحذف (عدم ظهور المناسبة للأوصاف المحذوفة (ويكفي للناظر) أن يقول ( بحثت فلم أجد) ويقبل قوله لعدالته (فإن قال المعترض الباقي كذلك) أي بحيث فلم أجد مناسبة (تعارضاً ووجب الترجيح بالبعدية وغيرها ولا يكلف المستدل بإثبات المناسبة بين الباقي والحكم (إذا لو أوجبنا على المعلل بيانها صار إخالة وهي مسلك آخر يكفي لإثبات المطلوب ابتداء (كذا في شرح المختصر . أقول) في ردّه لا بد أن يكون لا طريق الحذف شاملاً للباقي لئلا يلزم علية الباطل وطريق الحذف في هذه الصورة هو عدم ظهور المناسبة، فلا بد من أن لا يتحقق في الباقي فلا بد من ظهور المناسبة فيه كعدم الإلغاء والطرد أي كما أنه يجب ظهور عدم إلغاء الباقي كونه طردياً (فالمعترض) ليس معارضاً حتى يطلب الترجيح بل (ناقص) يقول : لو صح دليلكم لزم منه أن لا يكون الباقي علة لعدم وجود المناسبة فيه، فدليلكم باطل، وأيضاً الترجيح إنما يكون بعد الصلوح وههنا إذا أظهر المعترض عدم ظهور المناسبة للباقي فقد أبطل عليته، فأي شيء يرجح (تدبر . ثم إن كان كل من الحصر والإبطال قطعياً فالمسلك قطعي مقبول إجماعاً) ومثله ما إذا ثبت الحصر بخبر الواحد أو الإجماع السكوتي أو الأحادي، فإنه وإن كان ظنيناً لكنه مقبول عند الكل ( وإلا فظني مختلف فيه وفيه مذاهب ذهب (الأكثر) من الشافعية والمالكية إلى أنه (حجة للناظر والمناظر) زعماً منهم أنه يفيد ظن العلية، وكل ما كذلك هو يقبل (وعن الحنفية كلهم (إلا) الشيخ أبا بكر الجصاص (و) الشيخ (المرغيناني) هذا المسلك (ليس بحجة أصلا لا للناظر ولا للمناظر (لأن) الوصف (الباقي) بعد الحذف (لم يثبت اعتباره) شرعاً لظهور التأثير) ولا بدّ من ظهور التأثير شرعاً في الحجية والتأثير عندنا اعتبار نوع الوصف في نوع الحكم أو جنسه أو اعتبار جنسه في جنس الحكم أو نوعه، كما (ثالثها) مر أنه (حجة لهما) أي للناظر والمناظر ( إن أجمع على تعليل الأصل، وعليه الإمام إمام الحرمين، لأن الإجماع صار تعليل الأصل مقطوعاً، والمظنون فيما قطع بأصله واجب العمل دون غيره (رابعها) أنه (حجة للناظر لا للمناظر لعل وجه فرقهم أنه يفيد الظن للناظر، ولا يفيد للمناظر، فإن دعوى الحصر ليس إلا بحسب ظنه وظنه لا يكون حجة على الغير، لأن الأذهان خلقت متفاوته، فرب مقدمة يقبله بعض الأذهان دون آخر فكيف يكون ظنه حجة على غيره فافهم.
From this, the third method: al-sabr wa al-taqsim, which is enumerating the attributes suitable for being the cause and eliminating other than the claimed attribute, meaning invalidating it, so the claimed one is determined. Mere enumeration without attributing to the emergence of another attribute does not prevent it because the viewer claiming enumeration is upright, so his statement is accepted as he only judged after thorough investigation. If after investigation he does not find, he assumes enumeration, and the goal is not certainty so that it would be prevented after obtaining assumption, but there is hesitation in it, so reflect. And because the original is the absence of other attributes, and this is flimsier than a spider's web, as is obvious. Rather, enumeration is only prevented if it relies on presenting an attribute, so he must invalidate it to complete his evidence, and his disconnection from the research is not necessary according to the chosen opinion, because enumeration is presumptive, so there is no difficulty in the emergence of another attribute, given that the invalid attribute is like non-existent, so it does not harm enumeration, nor does the research disconnect in the Hashiyah. Al-Subki said: in my view it disconnects if the objection raised is equivalent to what he mentioned in the enumeration and invalidated. And in it, he can say: since it is equivalent to what I invalidated, what I mentioned? If you say: perhaps his purpose is that when he presented an equivalent attribute, he objected to the evidence of invalidation, so it is not correct to leave it for invalidation. I say: he can say: since it is invalid in my view, I left it. And now that you have presented, I roll up my sleeves for invalidation, so reflect. Then, from the methods of elimination: ilgha', which is stating the ruling with only the remaining attribute, without the partnership of another, in a locus that does not contain other attributes, so it is known that the eliminated has no part in the ruling by partnership with the remaining. If you say: the gist of this returns to that if the eliminated were a cause, the ruling would be absent with its absence, while the ruling is established with the absence of the eliminated attributes, so it would necessitate the condition of the converse. He answered: the converse is not necessary because what is meant here by ilgha' is negation of partiality, so its gist returns to that the eliminated is not a part of the remaining; otherwise the ruling would be established by it alone in this locus, so the converse does not follow. It only follows if one intends to invalidate the independence of the eliminated. It is said: if the remaining exists in a locus without the eliminated attributes, then analogy to that locus removes the burden of ilgha', so let them first analogize to it, and using sabr wa taqsim has no benefit. It is rebutted by saying that that analogy does not continue, as perhaps its attributes are more numerous than the supposed original, so to invalidate it, one must use division and elimination, leading to prolongation. And from the methods of elimination: tardi, which is stating that the attributes are casual, i.e., invalid, not considered by the Lawgiver either absolutely, i.e., entirely invalid in all rulings like length and shortness, or in the ruling under investigation like masculinity and femininity in rulings of manumission. And from the methods of elimination: lack of apparent suitability for the eliminated attributes, and it suffices for the viewer to say: I researched and did not find, and his statement is accepted due to his uprightness. If the objector says: the remaining is also such that I did not find suitability, they conflict and preponderance is required by posteriority and other factors, and the respondent is not burdened with proving suitability between the remaining and the ruling, because if we obligated him to demonstrate it, it would become ikhala, which is another method sufficient initially to prove the desired, as in Sharh al-Mukhtasar. I say in refutation: the method of elimination must not encompass the remaining, lest the validity of the invalid be necessitated. The method of elimination in this form is lack of apparent suitability, so it must not be realized in the remaining, so suitablity must appear in it, like the absence of ilgha' and tard, i.e., just as it is necessary for the absence of ilgha' of the remaining to be tardi. Thus the objector is not an opponent seeking preponderance, but is deficient, saying: if your evidence were correct, it would necessitate that the remaining is not a cause due to lack of suitablity in it, so your evidence is invalid. Moreover, preponderance only occurs after suitablity, and here if the objector shows lack of apparent suitablity for the remaining, he has invalidated its causality, so what is there to preponderate? Reflect. Then if both enumeration and invalidation are definitive, the method is definitive and accepted by consensus. Similarly if enumeration is established by khabar wahid or silent consensus or ahad, then although it is presumptive, it is accepted by all. Otherwise it is presumptive and disputed. There are schools: the majority of Shafi'is and Malikis hold that it is proof for the viewer and the opponent, claiming that it yields presumption of causality, and everything that does so is accepted. From the Hanafis, all except Abu Bakr al-Jassas and al-Marghinani hold that this method is not a proof at all, neither for the viewer nor the opponent, because the remaining attribute after elimination has not been established as valid by the Law due to lack of apparent effect, and effect must appear by Law for authority. Effect in our view is consideration of the type of attribute in the type of ruling or its genus, or consideration of its genus in the genus of ruling or its type. Third: it is said that it is proof for both if there is consensus on the reasoning of the original, according to Imam al-Haramayn, because consensus makes the reasoning of the original definitive, and what is presumptive in what is definitive in its root is obligatory to act upon, not others. Fourth: it is proof for the viewer, not for the opponent; perhaps the reason for their distinction is that it yields presumption for the viewer, but does not yield for the opponent, because the claim of enumeration is only according to his assumption, and his assumption is not proof against others, as minds are created varying, so perhaps a premise is accepted by some minds and not by another, so how can his assumption be proof against others? Understand.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the third method (maslak) of discovering the 'illa in qiyas: sabr wa taqsim (division and elimination). The author explains that this method involves listing all possible attributes that could be the 'illa and then eliminating those that are not suitable, leaving the claimed attribute as the 'illa. The discussion addresses objections: mere enumeration without evidence of a new attribute is acceptable from a trustworthy scholar after thorough investigation, as it yields presumption (zann). However, if an opponent presents an equally suitable attribute, the original enumerator must invalidate it. The passage then details three sub-methods of elimination: ilgha' (showing that the ruling exists without the eliminated attribute), tardi (proving the attribute is casually irrelevant), and lack of apparent munasaba (suitability) for the eliminated attributes. The text then discusses the hujjiyah (authoritativeness) of this method: it is definitive if both enumeration and invalidation are definitive; otherwise it is presumptive. The author presents four positions: (1) majority of Shafi'is and Malikis accept it as proof for both parties; (2) Hanafis except al-Jassas and al-Marghinani reject it entirely; (3) a third view accepts it if the reasoning of the original is based on consensus; (4) a fourth view accepts it only for the viewer, not the opponent, since presumption varies among individuals. The passage ends by emphasizing that the assumption of the viewer does not bind others.

Key Terms
السبر والتقسيم (al-sabr wa al-taqsim): Enumerating all attributes suitable for causality and eliminating those that are invalid to determine the true 'illa
الإلغاء (al-ilgha'): A method of elimination by showing the ruling exists with only the remaining attribute in a locus lacking other attributes
الطردية (al-tardiyya): Attributes that are casually irrelevant and not considered by the Lawgiver in any ruling or in a specific ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the general Hanafi position (excluding al-Jassas and al-Marghinani), why is sabr wa taqsim not a valid proof?
A) Because enumeration is always uncertain
B) Because the remaining attribute has not been proven valid by the Law due to lack of apparent effect
C) Because it requires consensus on the original ruling
D) Because it only benefits the viewer, not the opponent

Key Takeaway
Sabr wa taqsim is a presumptive method for discovering the 'illa, but Hanafis require apparent legal effect (ta'thir) for an attribute to be considered effective, making the method insufficient without independent evidence.

The Fourth Maslak: Munasabah and Ikhala
Defines munasabah and distinguishes agreed vs disputed types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between agreed munasabah (preserving the five universals) and disputed ikhala, and identify the Hanafi position on ikhala.

Core Idea
Munasabah is valid only when it preserves the five essentials; purely rational suitability (ikhala) is rejected by Hanafis.

In the Hanafi school, discovering the 'illa requires a valid method (maslak). The fourth maslak is munasabah, but not all munasabah is equal. This lesson defines the two types: the agreed-upon type that preserves the five essential universal needs, and the disputed type called ikhala, which Hanafis reject. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Recall the definition of munasabah
Munasabah is the suitability of an attribute to the ruling, often by attracting benefit or repelling harm. It is a method to establish the 'illa in qiyas.
The passage defines it briefly: 'its validity and effect are established by the Law.'
2
Identify the two categories of munasabah
The passage distinguishes: (1) munasabah that preserves the five necessary universals (din, nafs, aql, nasl, mal) - agreed upon by all schools; (2) munasabah not based on text or consensus - called ikhala or takhrij al-manat.
The five universals are the maqasid al-shari'ah.
3
Understand the condition for agreed munasabah
For munasabah to be valid, it must serve the preservation of the five essentials. This is accepted by Hanafis and others.
The attribute must be shown to protect these universals.
4
Analyze the dispute over ikhala
Ikhala is accepted by Shafi'is, Malikis, and Hanbalis because it yields strong presumption of causality. Hanafis generally reject it because the attribute lacks textual or consensus basis.
The passage does not give the final Hanafi position but notes the dispute.

Source Text

(و) المسلك الرابع المناسبة وقد مر تفسيرها وهي أن تثبت اعتبارها شرعاً وتأثيرها بالمعنى الذي مر ذكره كالمناسبات التي لحفظ الكليات الخمس الضرورية التي مرت حجة اتفاقاً بيننا وبين أصحاب المذاهب الثلاثة الباقية كما تقدم، وما ليس كذلك المناسب الذي لم يظهر اعتباره وتأثيره باعتبار الجنس والنوع لا بنص ولا إجماع وهو الإخالة، ويسمى تخريج المناط أيضاً حجة عند الشافعية بل المالكية أيضاً، بل الحنابلة أيضاً الحصول الظن بالعلية بإبداء المناسبة بين الحكم والوصف بأن يكون جالباً لنفع أو دافعاً لمضرة كالتحريم والإسكار فإنه مورث لمفسدة فيناسب التحريم لدفعها والظن واجب الاتباع، ثم اعلم أنه قد وقع لمشايخنا عبارات في تفسيرها منها إبداء مناسبة صالحة، لأن يضاف إليها
And the fourth method: munasabah (suitability), and its interpretation has already passed, and it is that its validity and effect are established by the Law in the sense mentioned before, like the suitabilities that preserve the five necessary universals which have passed, which are unanimously proof between us and the adherents of the remaining three schools as previously mentioned. And what is not like that is the suitable attribute whose validity and effect have not been shown by genus and type, neither by text nor by consensus, and that is al-ikhala, also called takhrij al-manat. It is proof according to the Shafi'is, and also the Malikis, and also the Hanbalis, for obtaining presumption of causality by presenting suitablity between the ruling and the attribute, such that it attracts a benefit or repels a harm, like prohibition and intoxication, for it causes corruption, so prohibition is suitable to repel it, and presumption is obligatory to follow. Then know that our scholars have expressions in its interpretation, including presenting a suitable attribute that is valid to be added to it.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage introduces the fourth method (maslak) of discovering the 'illa: munasabah (suitability). The author distinguishes between two types: (1) munasabah that preserves the five essential universals (the maqasid), which is agreed upon by all schools as a valid proof; (2) munasabah that is not based on text or consensus but on general suitability (al-munasaba al-mursala), called ikhala or takhrij al-manat. This second type is accepted by Shafi'is, Malikis, and Hanbalis because it yields presumption (zann) of causality, especially when it attracts benefit or repels harm, such as prohibiting intoxication because it leads to corruption. The Hanafi position is not explicitly stated here, but from the context and earlier discussion, Hanafis generally require explicit textual indication (al-munasaba al-mulaima) and do not accept purely rational suitability. The passage ends with a note that Hanafi scholars have various interpretations of ikhala.

Key Terms
المناسبة (al-munasabah): Suitability of an attribute to the ruling, often by attracting benefit or repelling harm
الإخالة (al-ikhala): A type of munasabah where the attribute's suitability is not based on text or consensus but on rational appeal to benefit or harm
الكليات الخمس (al-kulliyyat al-khams): The five necessary universals: preservation of religion, life, intellect, lineage, and property

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on ikhala (al-munasaba al-mursala)?
A) It is accepted as a valid method for determining 'illa
B) It is accepted only if based on consensus
C) It is generally not accepted because the attribute lacks textual or consensus basis
D) It is accepted for the viewer but not for the opponent

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts munasabah only when it is grounded in text or consensus; purely rational suitability (ikhala) is not a valid maslak for establishing 'illa.

The Four Views on Sabr wa Taqsim as Evidence for 'Illah
Discussion of four views on the probative value of sabr wa taqsim in qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four positions on the validity of sabr wa taqsim and apply the Hanafi critique to a proposed 'illah derived solely by elimination.

Core Idea
Sabr wa taqsim alone does not prove an 'illah unless the remaining attribute shows manifest effect.

This passage concludes the discussion on sabr wa taqsim (elimination), a method for determining the effective cause ('illah) in qiyas. The author first clarifies the procedure when the remaining attribute lacks apparent suitability, then categorizes the evidentiary value of the method into four views based on the certainty of the enumeration and the school of thought. Understanding these views is crucial for appreciating how Hanafis differ from Shafi'is and Malikis in qiyas methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic procedure of sabr wa taqsim
The investigator eliminates all unsuitable attributes from a set of possible causes until only one remains. He states 'I searched and did not find' and is accepted due to his reliability. If the objector claims the same for the remaining attribute, that is not an objection but a critique showing the arguer's proof is invalid.
The passage distinguishes between an opponent (muʿāriḍ) and a critic (nāqiḍ).
2
Distinguish definitive from probabilistic contexts
If both the enumeration (ḥaṣr) and the invalidation (ibṭāl) are definitive (qatʿī), the method is accepted by consensus. If based on probabilistic evidence like khabar al-wāḥid or ijma sukotī, it is also accepted. Otherwise, the method is probabilistic and disputed.
The passage here sets the stage for the four views.
3
State the four views and their proponents
View 1: Majority of Shafi'is and Malikis hold it is evidence for both investigator and disputant. View 2: Hanafis (except al-Jaṣṣāṣ and al-Marghīnānī) hold it is not evidence at all. View 3: Imām al-Ḥaramayn holds it is evidence if there is consensus on the ʿillah of the original. View 4: Some hold it is evidence for the investigator but not for the disputant.
Memorize the proponents for each view.
4
Analyze the Hanafi position
The Hanafi majority argue that mere elimination does not establish the remaining attribute's legal consideration (iʿtibār). Lack of observed suitability does not prove effectiveness; a text or clear indication is needed. This is the core critique.
The Hanafi requirement is that an ʿillah must have manifest effect (ẓuhūr al-athar).
5
Apply the distinction between sabr wa taqsim and ikhālah
Ikhālah is a separate method where suitability is posited without elimination. If sabr wa taqsim were accepted, it would blur into ikhālah, which Hanafis reject. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion.
The passage notes that requiring proof of suitability in sabr wa taqsim would make it ikhālah.

الحكم المبحوث عنه كالذكورة والأنوثة في أحكام العتق ومنها أي من طرق الحذف (عدم ظهور المناسبة للأوصاف المحذوفة (ويكفي للناظر) أن يقول ( بحثت فلم أجد) ويقبل قوله لعدالته (فإن قال المعترض الباقي كذلك) أي بحيث فلم أجد مناسبة (تعارضاً ووجب الترجيح بالبعدية وغيرها ولا يكلف المستدل بإثبات المناسبة بين الباقي والحكم (إذا لو أوجبنا على المعلل بيانها صار إخالة وهي مسلك آخر يكفي لإثبات المطلوب ابتداء (كذا في شرح المختصر . أقول) في ردّه لا بد أن يكون لا طريق الحذف شاملاً للباقي لئلا يلزم علية الباطل وطريق الحذف في هذه الصورة هو عدم ظهور المناسبة، فلا بد من أن لا يتحقق في الباقي فلا بد من ظهور المناسبة فيه كعدم الإلغاء والطرد أي كما أنه يجب ظهور عدم إلغاء الباقي كونه طردياً (فالمعترض) ليس معارضاً حتى يطلب الترجيح بل (ناقص) يقول : لو صح دليلكم لزم منه أن لا يكون الباقي علة لعدم وجود المناسبة فيه، فدليلكم باطل، وأيضاً الترجيح إنما يكون بعد الصلوح وههنا إذا أظهر المعترض عدم ظهور المناسبة للباقي فقد أبطل عليته، فأي شيء يرجح (تدبر . ثم إن كان كل من الحصر والإبطال قطعياً فالمسلك قطعي مقبول إجماعاً) ومثله ما إذا ثبت الحصر بخبر الواحد أو الإجماع السكوتي أو الأحادي، فإنه وإن كان ظنيناً لكنه مقبول عند الكل ( وإلا فظني) مختلف فيه وفيه مذاهب ذهب (الأكثر) من الشافعية والمالكية إلى أنه (حجة للناظر والمناظر) زعماً منهم أنه يفيد ظن العلية، وكل ما كذلك هو يقبل (وعن الحنفية كلهم (إلا) الشيخ أبا بكر الجصاص (و) الشيخ (المرغيناني) هذا المسلك (ليس بحجة أصلا لا للناظر ولا للمناظر (لأن) الوصف (الباقي) بعد الحذف (لم يثبت اعتباره) شرعاً لظهور التأثير) ولا بدّ من ظهور التأثير شرعاً في الحجية والتأثير عندنا اعتبار نوع الوصف في نوع الحكم أو جنسه أو اعتبار جنسه في جنس الحكم أو نوعه، كما (ثالثها) مر أنه (حجة لهما) أي للناظر والمناظر ( إن أجمع على تعليل الأصل، وعليه الإمام إمام الحرمين، لأن الإجماع صار تعليل الأصل مقطوعاً، والمظنون فيما قطع بأصله واجب العمل دون غيره (رابعها) أنه (حجة للناظر لا للمناظر لعل وجه فرقهم أنه يفيد الظن للناظر، ولا يفيد للمناظر، فإن دعوى الحصر ليس إلا بحسب ظنه وظنه لا يكون حجة على الغير، لأن الأذهان خلقت متفاوته، فرب مقدمة يقبله بعض الأذهان دون آخر فكيف يكون ظنه حجة على غيره فافهم.
The ruling under investigation, like masculinity and femininity in the rulings of emancipation. Among the methods of deletion is (the lack of apparent suitability for the deleted attributes. It is sufficient for the investigator to say: I searched and did not find. And his statement is accepted due to his reliability. If the objector says: the remaining is likewise (i.e., lacking suitability), then there is a conflict and preference must be given by remoteness and other factors, and the arguer is not required to prove suitability between the remaining attribute and the ruling. Because if we obliged the reasoner to explain it, it would become ikhālah, which is another method sufficient to prove the claim initially. This is as stated in Sharh al-Mukhtasar. I say in reply: The method of deletion must not encompass the remaining attribute else falsity would follow. The method of deletion in this case is the lack of apparent suitability, so it must not be realized in the remaining; rather suitability must be apparent in it. Like non-invalidity and containment. So the objector is not an opponent such that preference is sought, but rather a critic saying: if your proof were correct, it would necessitate that the remaining attribute is not effective due to lack of suitability, so your proof is invalid. Also, preference is only after suitability, and here when the objector shows lack of apparent suitability for the remaining, he has invalidated its effectiveness, so what is there to prefer? Reflect. Then if both enumeration and invalidation are definitive, then the method is definitive, accepted by consensus. Similarly, if enumeration is established by khabar al-wāḥid or tacit or aḥādī consensus, though it is probabilistic, it is accepted by all. Otherwise, it is probabilistic, disputed. There are schools: The majority of Shafi'is and Malikis hold it is evidence for both investigator and disputant, claiming it yields probability of effectiveness. And the Hanafis except Shaykh Abū Bakr al-Jaṣṣāṣ and Shaykh al-Marghīnānī: this method is not evidence at all, neither for investigator nor disputant, because the remaining attribute after deletion has not been established as considered legally due to lack of manifest effect. And effect according to us is the consideration of the type of attribute in the type of ruling or its genus, or its genus in the genus of ruling or its type. The third view: it is evidence for both if there is consensus on the reason of the original, according to Imām al-Ḥaramayn, because consensus makes the reason of the original definitive, and the probable when its origin is definitive is obligatory to act upon. The fourth view: it is evidence for the investigator but not for the disputant. The reason for their distinction is that it yields probability for the investigator but not for the disputant, because the claim of enumeration is only according to his opinion, and his opinion is not evidence against others, because minds are created differently, so a premise accepted by some minds may not be accepted by others. So how can his opinion be evidence against others? Understand.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion on the method of sabr wa taqsim (elimination), a key method for establishing the 'illah (effective cause) in qiyas. The author first clarifies that when the remaining attribute after deletion lacks apparent suitability, the investigator simply states that he found no suitability; his word is accepted due to his reliability. If the objector claims the same for the remaining attribute, then there is no conflict requiring preference; instead the objector is merely pointing out a flaw in the arguer's proof. The passage then categorizes the method's evidentiary value based on certainty: if the enumeration and invalidation are definitive (qat'i), the method is accepted by consensus. If based on probabilistic evidence (khabar al-wahid), it is also accepted. However, when the method is merely probabilistic, there is disagreement. The majority of Shafi'is and Malikis accept it as evidence for both parties, while Hanafis generally reject it, except al-Jaṣṣāṣ and al-Marghīnānī. A third view (Imam al-Haramayn) accepts it only if there is consensus on the 'illah of the original case, making the basis definitive. A fourth view accepts it for the investigator but not for the disputant, because the investigator's personal conclusion does not bind others. The Hanafi position emphasizes that the remaining attribute's legal consideration is not proven without manifest effect from the Lawgiver.

Key Terms
طريق الحذف (ṭarīq al-ḥadhf): A method of finding the 'illah by eliminating all unsuitable attributes until only one remains.
إخالة (ikhālah): A separate method where suitability is posited without explicit textual evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the majority Hanafi position (excluding al-Jaṣṣāṣ and al-Marghīnānī) on sabr wa taqsim?
A) It is evidence for both investigator and disputant
B) It is evidence for the investigator only
C) It is not evidence at all
D) It is evidence only if there is consensus on the original

Key Takeaway
Sabr wa taqsim is not a valid method for establishing 'illah in the Hanafi school unless the remaining attribute's legal consideration is independently proven.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
8 min
Ikhālah vs. Munāsabah: The Hanafi Rejection of Rational Suitability
Discussion of suitability method and the dispute over ikhālah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the difference between munāsabah and ikhālah, state the Hanafi position on ikhālah, and evaluate the Hanafi refutation of the Shafi'i argument.

Core Idea
Ikhālah fails because it yields only rational probability, not legal probability grounded in divine law.

This passage from Fawātih al-Raḥamūt explores the fourth method of establishing the effective cause ('illah) in qiyās: suitability (munāsabah). While suitability that preserves the five essentials is unanimously accepted, a more controversial type is ikhālah—suitability not confirmed by text or consensus. Here the author presents the positions of the schools, with the Hanafis firmly rejecting ikhālah as a valid source of evidence. Understanding this dispute is crucial for grasping the Hanafi methodological boundaries for analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Define the terms
First, clarify the definitions of munāsabah and ikhālah as given in the text. Munāsabah is suitability confirmed by text or consensus; ikhālah is suitability not so confirmed but inferred rationally.
Note the alternative term takhrīj al-manāṭ.
2
Identify the dispute
Determine who accepts ikhālah (Shafi'is, Malikis, Hanbalis) and who rejects it (Hanafis). The core issue is whether rational suitability alone can yield legal probability.
3
Analyze the Hanafi arguments
Examine the three main Hanafi counterarguments: (1) ikhālah is not necessarily what the Lawgiver intended; (2) there are examples where suitable attributes were disregarded (e.g., hardship of crafts vs. travel); (3) it resembles uncontrolled interests (maṣāliḥ mursalah) which are not evidence.
Pay careful attention to the example of ṣinā‘i shāqqa (difficult crafts).
4
Evaluate the rebuttal to the shabah objection
The text addresses a possible objection: that the Hanafi stance would undermine even genus-based suitability. Follow how the author responds: the established consideration of a genus creates a strong legal probability that a new type within that genus is also considered.
This response preserves the concept of maslak al-munāsabah while excluding ikhālah.

And the fourth method: suitability (al-munāsabah), whose explanation has passed, i.e., that its consideration legally and its effect are established in the sense previously mentioned. Like the suitabilities that preserve the five essentials, they are evidence by agreement between us and the three remaining schools, as previously. What is not like that, i.e., the suitable attribute whose consideration and effect have not appeared by genre and type without text or consensus, is ikhālah, also called takhrīj al-manāṭ. It is evidence according to the Shafi'is, indeed Malikis, indeed Hanbalis, because it yields probability of causality by presenting suitability between the ruling and the attribute, such as bringing benefit or repelling harm, like prohibition and intoxication, for it causes harm, so prohibition is suitable to repel it, and probability must be followed. Know that our scholars have statements in its interpretation, including presenting a suitable attribute fit to be attached to the ruling rationally, which is equivalent to what passed of presenting a precise attribute bringing benefit or repelling harm. Among them is what al-Qāḍī Imām Abū Zayd mentioned: if presented to sound minds, they would accept it. This also refers to what was mentioned, because acceptance is only for bringing benefit or repelling harm. Among them is from Imām al-Nasafī: the attribute being suggestive (mukhīl), i.e., creating an illusion of correctness in the heart. He said it is mere probability, which does not avail anything of truth, and its end is like inspiration, which is not valid as evidence, and because no one else knows it, so it is not evidence against others. Perhaps this commentator meant by suggestion what the mind suggests as correct, whether true or false, so he made his objection. However, proponents of suitability do not mean that; rather they mean by it being suggestive to the intellect that it has a suitability with the ruling such that the intellect accepts it and strongly conjectures it. It is not something that does not avail anything of truth, and its being like inspiration is not harmful, for it is one of God's proofs. Even if conceded, the difference is clear: inspiration is the occurrence of something in the mind that cannot be verified, unlike suitability. And that others do not know it is denied; rather it can be explained by bringing benefit or repelling harm. Contrary to the Hanafis, they do not accept ikhālah at all because, although it yields probability, it is not necessary for the Lawgiver to have established it based on that, nor is it probable that He established it due to frequent violations, like in the case of suitable attributes known to be disregarded, such as difficult crafts: they are more suitable for alleviation than the hardship of travel, but the law considered the second and ignored the first. And the uncontrolled interests (maṣāliḥ mursalah) are also suitable, but not considered legally. When it does not yield probability of the Lawgiver's consideration, it is not a legal evidence; it is mere intellectual fancies, so not considered. Perhaps this is what Imām al-Nasafī meant by it being mere probability, i.e., it is not probability of the Lawgiver's consideration, so it does not avail anything of truth. If you say: ikhālah definitely yields probability, and consensus has been formed on acting upon probability. He said: Consensus on acting upon probability is only on the assumption that it is legal probability, obtained from the Lawgiver's side and probability of His consideration. Then here is a discussion: If what was mentioned is complete, then it would follow that what has its genus's effect shown in the genus of the ruling would not be evidence at all, because only a type of it in a type of ruling has appeared from the law, and it does not necessitate the effect of a type in another type of ruling. So nothing remains but mere probability, which does not avail anything of truth. And in the mursal mulā'im it is more apparent. So your answer is our answer. Perhaps the truth is not hidden from the intelligent: since suitability indicates fitness for causality and the Lawgiver's consideration of its genus in the genus of ruling or its type is established, a strong probability of His consideration of it arises. This probability arises from the law and relates to the Lawgiver's consideration. Denying this is perhaps obstinacy. The mere possibility of non-consideration of another type does not harm our claim, for the claim is strong legal probability, and possibility does not harm it. Understand. As for their argument that takhrīj al-manāṭ is never free from opposition: just as the reasoner says 'I presented it to my intellect and it accepted it,' similarly the opponent says 'My intellect did not accept it when presented.' If it were valid, it contains an indication that it is not valid because he can present the aspect of suitability and the intellect accepts it, and the opponent cannot then say 'my intellect did not accept it.' This indicates only the denial of evidence regarding others, as al-Qāḍī Imām Abū Zayd says, and it does not necessitate absolute denial of evidence. And the claimant is less than that. Understand. Note: Ash-Shabah (resemblance) is what is not suitability in itself, but gives the illusion of suitability, and that illusion is only...
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth method of establishing the 'illah: suitability (al-munāsabah). Suitability that preserves the five essential objectives (maqāṣid) is accepted by all schools. The dispute concerns the type of suitability not explicitly confirmed by text or consensus, called ikhālah or takhrīj al-manāṭ. The Shafi'is, Malikis, and Hanbalis accept it because it yields a strong probability of causality based on achieving benefit or preventing harm. The Hanafis reject it entirely for several reasons: (1) it is not necessarily what the Lawgiver intended, (2) there are instances where suitable attributes are disregarded by the Law, e.g., the hardship of crafts is more suitable for concession than travel hardship, but only the latter was given, (3) it resembles uncontrolled interests (maṣāliḥ mursalah) which are not legally recognized. The Hanafis argue that probability must be legal probability (ẓann shar‘ī), i.e., arising from the Lawgiver's indications, not from mere rational speculation. The passage also addresses a counterargument: if we accept the genus-level suitability, then why not accept any type? It responds that the established genus effect creates a strong legal probability. Finally, the passage distinguishes shabah (resemblance) from true suitability: shabah merely gives an illusion of suitability but is not genuine.

Key Terms
مناسبة (munāsabah): Suitability between an attribute and a ruling, such that the attribute brings benefit or repels harm.
إخالة (ikhālah): A suitable attribute not confirmed by text or consensus but deemed effective by rational inference (also called takhrīj al-manāṭ).
مصلحة مرسلة (maṣlaḥah mursalah): Unregulated public interest not explicitly considered by the Lawgiver.
ظن شرعي (ẓann shar‘ī): Legal probability arising from indications in the divine law, as opposed to mere rational speculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do Hanafis reject ikhālah (takhrīj al-manāṭ) as a method for establishing the 'illah?
A) It does not yield any form of probability.
B) It contradicts the consensus of the Companions.
C) It does not produce legal probability (ẓann shar‘ī) and there are cases where rational suitability was disregarded by the Lawgiver.
D) It is only accepted by the Shafi'is.

Key Takeaway
Hanafis reject ikhālah because it yields rational probability, not legal probability (ẓann shar‘ī), and the Lawgiver's actual consideration is the only valid basis for establishing an effective cause.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
12 min
The Validity of Ikhala as a Method for 'Illa
Dispute on whether ikhala is a valid method for 'illa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafis reject al-ikhala as a valid method for determining the 'illa and distinguish between legal conjecture (zann shar'i) and mere suitability.

Core Idea
Ikhala (subjective suitability) does not produce legal conjecture because the Shari'ah may ignore suitable attributes.

This lesson explores a critical dispute in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: whether the appropriateness (ikhala) of a description for a ruling is sufficient to establish it as the effective cause ('illa) in qiyas. While some schools accept ikhala as producing strong conjecture, Hanafis require the conjecture to be legal (zann shar'i) – arising from a Shari'ah indication, not merely from human intellect. Understanding this distinction is key to applying qiyas correctly within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Define ikhala and munasaba
Start by clearly defining the two key terms: al-ikhala (appropriateness that creates an illusion of validity) and al-munasaba (suitability that brings benefit or repels harm). Notice that Hanafis distinguish between mere logical suitability and suitability recognized by the Shari'ah.
The passage also mentions 'al-zann al-shar'i' – legal conjecture – as the only valid basis for 'illa.
2
State the Hanafi rejection and its rationale
Identify the Hanafi position: ikhala is rejected as a method for 'illa. Their proof is that the Shari'ah sometimes ignores suitable attributes (e.g., the hardship of crafts is more deserving of leniency than travel, yet travel gets rukhsa while crafts do not). Also, unrestricted interests (masalih mursala) are not considered.
This shows that mere suitability does not guarantee consideration by the Lawgiver.
3
Follow the opposing view's argument
The proponents of munasaba (including Shafi'is) argue that ikhala produces strong conjecture, sound intellects accept it, and it can be explained to others. They liken it to other proofs like istihsan.
Imam al-Nasafi is quoted as dismissing ikhala as mere illusion, but the commentator refines this.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response on legal conjecture
The Hanafi response emphasizes that the conjecture from ikhala is not 'zann shar'i' – it does not arise from a Shari'ah indication. The commentator argues that legal conjecture must be based on evidence that the Shari'ah actually considered that attribute. The possibility of non-consideration (ihtimal al-ilgha) is enough to undermine the claim.
The text also addresses the objection about takhrij al-manat and opposing views: the proponent can objectively demonstrate suitability, so the opponent's rejection is only personal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ظن، يعني إنه ليس ظن اعتبار الشارع فهو لا يغني من الحق شيئاً. فإن قلت : الإخالة تفيد الظن البتة والإجماع انعقد على اعتبار الظن قال : (والإجماع على العمل بالظن إنما هو على تقدير كونه) أي الظن (شرعياً) اعتبار الشارع جنسها في جنس الحكم أو نوعه حدث ظن اعتباره إياه ظناً قوياً، وهذا الظن حادث من الشرع ومتعلق باعتبار الشارع وإنكار هذا عسى أن يكون مكابرة، ومطلق احتمال عدم اعتبار نوع آخر لا يضر مدعانا فإن The fourth principle: Qiyas. The ruling is referred to reason, and it is equal. And because there passed from mentioning a precise description that brings benefit or repels harm, and among them is what the chief judge Abu Zayd mentioned: if it is presented to sound intellects, they accept it. This also refers to what was mentioned, for acceptance is only for bringing benefit or repelling harm. And among them is from Imam al-Nasafi: the description being appropriate (mukhīl), i.e., creating in the heart an illusion of soundness. He said it is mere conjecture (zann) which does not avail against truth at all, and its utmost is to make it like inspiration (ilhām), which is not a valid proof, and because no one else can know it, so it cannot be a proof against others. Perhaps this one meant by 'imagining' what the mind imagines as correct, whether correct or corrupt, so he raised what he raised. But the proponents of suitability (munāsaba) do not mean that; rather they mean by it being appropriate in the mind that it has a suitability with the ruling such that the mind accepts it and conjectures strongly, and it is not that which does not avail against truth at all. And its being like inspiration does not harm, for it is a proof from Allah's proofs. And even if conceded, the difference is clear: inspiration is something occurring in the mind that cannot be verified, by evidence unlike suitability, and lack of access for others is denied; rather it can be explained by bringing benefit or repelling harm. (Contrary to the Hanafis) for they do not accept ikhāla at all (because it), although it benefits conjecture, it is not necessitative of the Lawgiver's placing the ruling upon it, nor is it conjectured that He placed it because it often diverges, as in the suitable that is known to be nullified, like difficult crafts, for they are more suitable for leniency than the hardship of travel, but the Shari'ah considered the second and ignored the first. And the unrestricted interests (masālih mursala) are also suitable but not considered by the Shari'ah. And if it does not produce conjecture of the Lawgiver's consideration, it is not a legal proof; it is merely mental whims, so not considered. Perhaps this is what Imam al-Nasafi meant: it is mere conjecture, i.e., it is not conjecture of the Lawgiver's consideration, so it does not avail against truth at all. If you say: ikhāla definitely benefits conjecture and consensus has been reached on considering conjecture. He said: (Consensus on acting on conjecture is only on the condition that it is) i.e., the conjecture (legal) obtained from the Shari'ah and conjecture of the Lawgiver's consideration. This is it. Then there is a research here: if what was mentioned were complete, it would necessitate that what appears of the effect of its genus in the genus of the ruling would not be a proof at all, for only a type of it appeared from the Shari'ah in a type of the ruling, and the effect of a type in another type of the ruling does not follow. Nothing remains but mere conjecture, which does not avail against truth at all. And in the unrestricted (mursal) that is suitable, it is more apparent. So your answer is our answer. Perhaps the truth is not hidden from the intelligent, for when suitability indicates its suitability for causality and the Shari'ah's consideration of its genus in the genus of the ruling or its type is established, a strong conjecture of its consideration occurs, and this conjecture arises from the Shari'ah and relates to the Lawgiver's consideration. Denying this may be stubbornness. And the absolute possibility of non-consideration of another type does not harm our claim, for the claimant claims strong legal conjecture, and possibility does not harm it. So understand. (As for their argument that) i.e., takhrīj al-manāt (cannot be free from opposition, since) as the reasoner says: I presented it to my intellect and it accepted it, likewise (the opponent says: my intellect did not accept it) when presented. If it were complete, there is indication that it is not complete, because he can present the aspect of suitability and the intellect accepts it, and the opponent cannot then say: my intellect did not accept it. (It only indicates the negation of proof for others as the chief judge Abu Zayd says, and negation of proof completely does not follow from it, and the claimant claims less than that. So understand.)
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is a dispute about whether الإخالة (appropriateness) is a valid method for determining the 'illa (effective cause) in qiyas. The commentator begins by defining المناسبة (suitability) as a description that brings benefit or repels harm, and presents two opinions: that of القاضي الإمام أبو زيد, who says that a sound intellect naturally accepts it, and that of الإمام النسفي, who dismisses it as mere conjecture akin to inspiration. The commentator then defends the proponents of suitability, arguing that it produces strong conjecture and can be explained to others, unlike inspiration. The Hanafi position is that الإخالة is rejected because it does not guarantee that the Shari'ah would use it; examples are given of suitable attributes that were ignored by the Lawgiver, such as the hardship of crafts versus travel, and unrestricted interests. The commentator refutes the claim that الإخالة is pure conjecture by distinguishing between general conjecture and legal conjecture that arises from the Shari'ah. Finally, the argument that تخريج المناط is subject to opposing views is addressed: the proponent can demonstrate suitability objectively, so the opponent's claim of rejection is not valid; it only negates proof for that particular opponent, not the method's validity in principle.

Key Terms
الإخالة (al-ikhāla): A description that creates an illusion of suitability for the 'illa in the heart.
المناسبة (al-munāsaba): A description that is suitable for the ruling, bringing benefit or repelling harm, and accepted by sound intellect.
الظن الشرعي (al-zann al-shar'ī): Conjecture that arises from a Shari'ah indication and relates to the Lawgiver's consideration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis reject الإخالة as a valid method for determining the 'illa?
A) Because it is based on pure speculation without textual support.
B) Because it is not mentioned in the Qur'an.
C) Because they prefer qiyas over other methods.
D) Because it always leads to contradictory results.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rejection of ikhala underscores the requirement that the 'illa in qiyas must be based on a Shari'ah indication, not merely on rational suitability.
